###begin article-title 0
###xml 29 39 29 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 90 95 90 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 16 21 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Analysis of the mouse mutant Cloth-ears shows a role for the voltage-gated sodium channel Scn8a in peripheral neural hearing loss
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 235 236 235 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
###xml 243 244 243 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
###xml 367 377 367 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 379 383 379 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 386 396 386 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 664 674 652 662 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 737 746 725 734 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 751 757 739 745 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 823 832 811 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 946 952 934 940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 957 966 945 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 1075 1085 1063 1073 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 1179 1184 1163 1168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1364 1369 1348 1353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1435 1445 1419 1429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 1495 1500 1479 1484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 48 54 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 105 110 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 291 296 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 353 358 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 397 401 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 675 679 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 758 762 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 833 837 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 967 971 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1370 1375 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Deafness is the most common sensory disorder in humans and the aetiology of genetic deafness is complex. Mouse mutants have been crucial in identifying genes involved in hearing. However, many deafness genes remain unidentified. Using N-ethyl N-nitrosourea (ENU) mutagenesis to generate new mouse models of deafness, we identified a novel semi-dominant mouse mutant, Cloth-ears (Clth). Cloth-ears mice show reduced acoustic startle response and mild hearing loss from approximately30 days old. Auditory-evoked brainstem response (ABR) and distortion product otoacoustic emission (DPOAE) analyses indicate that the peripheral neural auditory pathway is impaired in Cloth-ears mice, but that cochlear function is normal. In addition, both Clth/Clth and Clth/+ mice display paroxysmal tremor episodes with behavioural arrest. Clth/Clth mice also show a milder continuous tremor during movement and rest. Longitudinal phenotypic analysis showed that Clth/+ and Clth/Clth mice also have complex defects in behaviour, growth, neurological and motor function. Positional cloning of Cloth-ears identified a point mutation in the neuronal voltage-gated sodium channel alpha-subunit gene, Scn8a, causing an aspartic acid to valine (D981V) change six amino acids downstream of the sixth transmembrane segment of the second domain (D2S6). Complementation testing with a known Scn8a mouse mutant confirmed that this mutation is responsible for the Cloth-ears phenotype. Our findings suggest a novel role for Scn8a in peripheral neural hearing loss and paroxysmal motor dysfunction.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 719 729 719 729 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b48">Steel 1995</xref>
###xml 805 824 805 824 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b8">Cohen &amp; Gorlin 1995</xref>
###xml 1007 1026 1007 1026 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b1">Atar &amp; Avraham 2005</xref>
###xml 1028 1039 1028 1039 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b18">Holley 2005</xref>
###xml 1547 1553 1547 1553 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1541 1558 1541 1558 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b2">Brown <italic>et al.</italic> 2008</xref>
###xml 1720 1742 1720 1742 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b39">Parkinson &amp; Brown 2002</xref>
###xml 97 105 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">children</span>
###xml 165 171 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 205 211 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 487 491 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 496 502 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 1336 1341 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1424 1429 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1525 1530 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1575 1580 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1631 1636 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Profound or severe hearing impairment affects around 1 in 1000 live births and another 1 in 1000 children suffer hearing loss before adulthood. Approximately 30% of humans over the age of 65 and 40-50% of humans over the age of 75 are affected by hearing loss [National Institute on Deafness and Other Communication Disorders (NIDCD, )]. Defects in the external, middle and inner ears and the peripheral neural and central auditory processing systems can result in hearing impairment in mice and humans. Pathological causes include morphological defects of the middle and inner ears, developmental and functional defects of cochlear components and neural defects in peripheral audition and central auditory processing (Steel 1995). Genetic factors are estimated to cause around 50% of all deafness cases (Cohen & Gorlin 1995); therefore, uncovering the genetic pathways involved in hearing and deafness is crucial to the development of therapies that either prevent or correct deafness causing pathologies (Atar & Avraham 2005; Holley 2005). However, the aetiology of genetic deafness is complex. A large number of genes involved in hearing and/or deafness have been identified (see Hereditary Hearing Loss homepage: ). Estimates vary but it seems likely that several hundred genes may be involved in the hearing process. Not only have mouse models have been crucial in identifying many of these genes, but in addition many mouse mutants have recapitulated the variety of pathologies, age of onset and mode of inheritance of human deafness (Brown et al. 2008). Comparison of human deafness loci and the map positions of known deaf mouse mutants shows that many loci do not have a comparative locus in the other species (Parkinson & Brown 2002), emphasizing that a large number of genes remain to be discovered. In particular, the genetics of peripheral neural hearing, central auditory processing, late-onset and noise-induced hearing loss is still poorly understood.
###end p 2
###begin p 3
###xml 82 83 82 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
###xml 90 91 90 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
###xml 145 151 145 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 139 156 139 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b36">Nolan <italic>et al.</italic> 2000</xref>
###xml 202 212 202 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 214 218 214 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 295 304 295 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 602 612 602 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 779 784 775 780 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 844 849 840 845 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 999 1004 995 1000 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1111 1116 1107 1112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 110 115 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 220 225 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 305 309 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 881 886 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1064 1068 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1072 1078 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 1217 1222 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
To identify novel genes involved in hearing loss, we used the resources of the UK N-ethyl N-nitrosourea (ENU) mouse mutagenesis programme (Nolan et al. 2000). One mutant generated from this screen, the Cloth-ears (Clth) mouse, was identified by its poor startle response to sound. We found that Clth/Clth mice have mild but discernable hearing loss [+12 dB sound pressure level (SPL) threshold shift]. Auditory-evoked brainstem response (ABR) and distortion product otoacoustic emission (DPOAE) analysis indicated that this hearing loss is of peripheral neural (retrocochlear) origin. Furthermore, the Cloth-ears mutant has additional motor symptoms. Mapping and candidate gene sequencing showed a novel mutation in the neuronal voltage-gated sodium channel (VGSC) alpha-subunit Scn8a, causing a non-synonymous change in the SCN8A peptide. The Scn8a gene is mutated in at least 11 mouse mutants, which show a range of motor dysfunction including paralysis, dystonia and tremor. However, mutation in Scn8a has never been shown to cause hearing impairment in either mice or humans. Here, we show that mutation in Scn8a is associated with peripheral neural hearing impairment and paroxysmal motor dysfunction in a novel mouse mutant and suggest a role for SCN8A in these processes.
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Methods
###end title 4
###begin title 5
Animals and complementation testing
###end title 5
###begin p 6
###xml 232 242 226 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 368 378 362 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 400 410 394 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 470 480 464 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 536 542 530 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 593 599 587 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 606 614 600 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vitro</italic>
###xml 791 796 785 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 797 798 791 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">J</italic>
###xml 796 798 790 792 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4<italic>J</italic></sup>
###xml 838 843 832 837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 997 1002 991 996 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1003 1004 997 998 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">J</italic>
###xml 1002 1004 996 998 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4<italic>J</italic></sup>
###xml 1038 1043 1032 1037 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1043 1047 1037 1041 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1043 1047 1037 1041 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 97 101 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 124 128 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 243 247 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 481 485 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 600 604 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 801 805 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1009 1013 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1050 1054 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1247 1251 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Mice were kept on a 12-h-light, 12-h-dark cycle at 19-23degreesC and 45-65% humidity. Up to four mice were housed per cage. Mice were fed SDS 3ME (Special Diet Services, Witham, Essex, UK) pellets and chlorine sterilized water. All Cloth-ears mice were bred in-house and genotyped using standard polymerase chain reaction (PCR) methods once a genetic map position for Cloth-ears was established. The Cloth-ears founder arose on a BALB/cAnN x C3H/HeH genetic background. Cloth-ears mice were generated by backcross breeding of genotyped Clth/+ to C3H/HeH or by intercross breeding of genotyped Clth/+ mice. In vitro fertilization (IVF) procedures were carried out by the MRC Harwell Frozen Embryo and Sperm Archive (FESA) core. For complementation testing, cryopreserved sperm from C57BL/6J- Scn8a4J/J mice carrying the N1370T mutation in Scn8a was obtained from the Jackson Laboratory (stock number 004102) and rederived by IVF and maintained by backcross on the C57BL/6 strain. Several C57BL/6J- Scn8a4J/J/+ mice were mated to confirmed Scn8aClth/+ mice, and the offspring from several litters were examined for abnormal phenotypes (including tremor, gait defects, hindlimb dragging and paralysis) every 2 days from birth until 21 days old, when mice were culled for welfare reasons.
###end p 6
###begin title 7
Genetic mapping
###end title 7
###begin p 8
###xml 1310 1319 1310 1319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a_SNP</italic>
###xml 1388 1397 1388 1397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a_SNP</italic>
###xml 1407 1408 1407 1408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
###xml 20 25 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 190 195 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
###xml 257 262 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
DNA extraction from mouse tissues and PCR amplification were performed under standard protocols. Annotated polymorphic markers were identified from public databases [microsatellite markers: Mouse Genome Informatics (MGI), Broad Institute Genetic Map of the Mouse Genome (Whitehead/MIT) and Center for Inherited Disease Research (CIDR); single nucleotide polymorphism (SNP) markers: Ensembl, Genomics Institute of the Novartis Research Foundation website (GNF)] and were tested for polymorphism in the parental strains BALB/cAnN and C3H/HeH. Polymerase chain reaction of microsatellite amplicons for low-resolution mapping was performed using one fluorescently labelled primer per reaction. Polymerase chain reaction products were analysed on 6% acrylamide gels on an ABI Prism 377 DNA sequencer and 377 XL DNA sequencer Data Collection (version 2.6) software. Results were analysed using ABI Prism GeneScan Analysis software (version 3.7.1) and ABI Prism Genotyper software (version 3.7). For high-resolution mapping, polymorphic microsatellite and SNP amplicons were analysed on 6% acrylamide gels using the single-stranded conformational polymorphism (SSCP) method and by pyrosequencing on a PSQ HS 96A pyrosequencer (Biotage) using one biotinylated primer per reaction. Primers used for the in-house marker Scn8a_SNP were forward: AGCTAATAAGCAAGGAGG; reverse: CACCTATGACTAAGCTAGCC and Scn8a_SNP: CAGCAGCCNCTATGTCTCTTT.
###end p 8
###begin title 9
Candidate gene assessment and mutation screening
###end title 9
###begin p 10
###xml 499 508 499 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 88 93 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 262 267 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 344 349 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 393 396 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Man</span>
###xml 398 402 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">OMIM</span>
###xml 509 513 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Candidate genes mapping to the non-recombinant region were identified using the Ensembl mouse genome database (versions 30, 32 and 33) and assessed for candidacy by expression and function [MGI, GeneCards database, version 2.31 (Weizmann Institute of Science)], mouse mutants [MGI, Transgenic/Targeted Mutation database (TBASE)] and associated human disorders [Online Mendelian Inheritance of Man (OMIM)]. Exonic and splice-site sequence from candidate genes was amplified from genomic DNA from two Clth/Clth mice and the two parental strains BALB/cAnN and C3H/HeH, and was sequenced under standard protocols. Sequences were examined for integrity using the ABIPrism EditView ABI Automated DNA Sequence Viewer (version 1.0.1) viewer programme and analysed for mutation using DNAStar Lasergene (v6.0) sequence analysis software.
###end p 10
###begin title 11
Peptide predictions
###end title 11
###begin p 12
###xml 136 146 136 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 355 365 355 365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 21 26 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 40 45 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 242 247 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Peptide sequences of mouse SCN8A, other mouse SCN-alpha peptides and SCN8A orthologues were obtained from Ensembl. Wild-type and mutant Cloth-ears peptide sequences were predicted and compared using EditSeq computer software (DNAStar). Other mouse SCN peptides and SCN8A orthologues were aligned using clustal-W web-based software (). The position of the Cloth-ears mutant amino acid in the SCN8A protein was determined using putative predicted protein domains from Ensembl and UniProt databases.
###end p 12
###begin title 13
Analysis of auditory function
###end title 13
###begin title 14
Assessment of the acoustic startle response
###end title 14
###begin p 15
###xml 1115 1120 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1171 1175 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Clickbox (Institute of Hearing Research, Nottingham, UK) and quantitative startlebox (acoustic startle) (SmithKline Beecham Pharmaceuticals, plc.) protocols were carried out as outlined on the EMPRESS website (). During clickbox testing, a quick backwards flick of the ear pinna (the Preyer's reflex) and a rapid 'jump' or contraction of the neck and trunk muscles (the startle response) was recorded as a normal response. A lack of either the Preyer's reflex or startle response, or a markedly milder response of either reflexes, was recorded as a reduced response. A complete lack of both reflexes was recorded as no response. In startlebox (acoustic startle) analysis, the maximal startle amplitude and the latency of the maximal startle to 110 dB SPL, white noise, 40 ms tone bursts, and of background movement, was recorded. Mean gross startle amplitudes were calculated from 10 startle trials, mean basal movement was calculated from 10 recordings in the absence of a soundburst and mean startle amplitudes were calculated by subtracting the mean basal movement from the mean gross startle amplitude for each mouse. Amplitude and latency of the startle response of mice was measured using Windows 3.1 software.
###end p 15
###begin title 16
Auditory-evoked brainstem response (ABR) analysis
###end title 16
###begin p 17
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 1753 1757 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Mice were anaesthetized with ketamine (Ketasettrade mark) and additionally given medetomidine (Domitortrade mark) for muscle relaxation and analgesia by intraperitoneal injection (0.5 ml Domitortrade mark at 100 mg/ml with 4.12 ml water and 0.38 ml Ketasettrade mark at 1 mg/ml; administered at a rate of 0.1 ml/10 g of body weight). Animals were placed in an audiometric chamber (IAC 401-A-SE) on a heated mat (approximately 37degreesC) to maintain body temperature. Acoustic stimuli were delivered monaurally to the right ear at a distance of 1.5 cm via a free field transducer [ES1 Tucker Davis Technology (TDT), Alachua, FL, USA], controlled by SigGen/BioSig software (TDT), using TDT system III hardware. The transducer was calibrated using a 1 4" measuring microphone (7016 ACO-Pacific, Belmont, CA, USA) and SigCal software (TDT). Electrodes (Grass Telefactor F-E2-12) were placed subdermally over the vertex (active), right mastoid (reference) and left mastoid (ground). The response from the electrodes was recorded for a period of 10 ms, over a total of 312 repetitions, and amplified using TDT system III hardware. The repetitions were averaged and bandpass filtered between 300 and 1500 Hz, using the BioSig software. Tone burst stimuli totalled 7 ms duration including 1 ms rise/fall time, and were presented at a rate of 21/s starting at 90 dB SPL followed by decreasing steps of 10 dB until 50 dB SPL, and in 5 dB steps from 45 to 5 dB SPL, until a threshold was reached. Threshold estimation was determined visually by the lack of replicable peak morphology in the response trace. Frequencies used were tone bursts at 8, 12, 20 and 26 kHz for threshold determination and at 8, 12, 20 and 32 kHz for analysis of peak latency. Recovery of mice was accelerated by administration of atipamezole (Antisedantrade mark, 5 mg/ml) at the rate of 1 mg/kg of body weight.
###end p 17
###begin title 18
Distortion product otoacoustic emission (DPOAE) analysis
###end title 18
###begin p 19
###xml 434 441 434 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 906 907 906 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 907 908 907 908 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 962 963 962 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 963 964 963 964 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 998 999 998 999 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 999 1000 999 1000 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1119 1120 1119 1120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 1120 1121 1120 1121 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1144 1145 1144 1145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 1145 1146 1145 1146 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 1147 1148 1147 1148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 1148 1149 1148 1149 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1211 1212 1211 1212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 1212 1213 1212 1213 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1214 1215 1214 1215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 1215 1216 1215 1216 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
Mice were anesthetized with ketamine (0.12 mg per g of body weight, i.p.) and xylazine (0.01 mg per g, i.p.). Sound was delivered via a probe with its tip within 1 mm of the tympanic membrane and coupled to a closed acoustic system comprising two MicroTech Gefell 1 inch MK102 microphones for delivering tones and a Bruel & Kjaer 3135 1/4 inch microphone for monitoring sound pressure at the tympanum. The sound system was calibrated in situ in dB SPL for frequencies between 1 and 70 kHz. The position of the coupler was adjusted to minimize peaks and dips in the calibration curve. White noise and tone pulses with rise-fall times of 0.2 ms were synthesized by a Data Translation 3010 data acquisition board, attenuated and used for sound system calibration and acoustic stimulation. Data were digitized at 250 kHz and stored on a PC. Distortion product otoacoustic emissions were measured for levels of f1 ranging from 10 to 80 dB SPL, with the levels of the f2 tone set 10 dB below that of the f1 tone. Distortion product otoacoustic emission threshold curves were constructed from measurements of the level of the f1 tone that produced a 2f1-f2 DPOAE with a level of 0 dB SPL, where the frequency ratio of f2/f1 was 1.23. System distortion during DPOAE measurements was 80 dB below the primary tone levels.
###end p 19
###begin title 20
Histological analysis
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 358 359 358 359 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sc>
###xml 448 449 448 449 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sc>
###xml 546 547 540 541 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sc>
###xml 1342 1343 1335 1336 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sc>
###xml 1406 1407 1398 1399 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sc>
###xml 1501 1502 1492 1493 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">m</sc>
###xml 4 8 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
All mice examined by histological methods were sex matched with littermate controls. Ossicles were dissected, placed into formalin solution and examined by X-ray analysis using Faxitron equipment (Qados Ltd, Sandhurst, Berkshire, UK). For examination of cochlear hair cells, brains were removed and bisected heads were placed into 2.5% glutaraldehyde in 0.1 m phosphate buffer. Cochleae were dissected and fixed in fresh 2.5% glutaraldehyde in 0.1 m phosphate buffer for 4-5 h, rotating, at 4degreesC, and then washed four times for 5 min in 0.1 m phosphate buffer. The bony shell of the cochlea was then removed. Samples were processed by dehydrating, critical point drying and gold sputter coating at the Electron Microscopy Unit, Royal Holloway University of London, Egham, Surrey TW20 0EX. Ultrastructural analysis of cochlear hair cells was carried out using Hitachi S-2400 and S-3000N scanning electron microscopes. Necropsy and histological analysis was carried out as outlined on the EMPReSS website (). For cerebellar histopathology, brains were removed and snap-frozen on dry ice in Optimal Cutting Temperature (OCT) mounting medium (VWR). Fifteen micrometre parasagittal cryosections were cut on a microtome, mounted on Superfrost Plus slides (BDH) and stained in 0.5% cresyl violet solution. For cell counts and measurements, 5 mum coronal wax sections from fixed brains were taken every 100 mum through the cerebellum and stained with cresyl violet. Five matched sections (spanning 400 mum) were used for Purkinje cell counts and measurements at three regions in the anterior (containing predominantly lobes I-VI), posterior (lobes VII-IX) and midway between these selected regions, posterior to the primary fissure (lobes VI and X). Cells were counted if the nuclei could be visualized. Maximum width of the sections (discounting the paraflocculus) and distance from the top of the cerebellum to the fourth ventricle or medulla at the base of the cerebellar vermis were also measured. The ratio between the width Purkinje cell layer (PCL) and granule cell layer (GCL) was calculated by measuring matched regions in the cerebellar hemispheres in all sections.
###end p 21
###begin title 22
Phenotypic and behavioural testing
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 20 25 20 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 25 29 25 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 25 29 25 29 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 36 41 36 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 41 45 41 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 41 45 41 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 46 51 46 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 51 55 51 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 51 55 51 55 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 90 95 90 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 95 99 95 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 95 99 95 99 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 296 302 296 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 289 308 289 308 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b44">Rogers <italic>et al.</italic> (1997</xref>
###xml 871 876 871 876 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 876 880 876 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 876 880 876 880 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 881 886 881 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 886 890 886 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 886 890 886 890 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 910 915 910 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 915 919 915 919 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 915 919 915 919 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 966 967 966 967 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1001 1007 1001 1007 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5</xref>
###xml 1242 1247 1242 1247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1247 1251 1247 1251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1247 1251 1247 1251 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1258 1263 1258 1263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1263 1267 1263 1267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1263 1267 1263 1267 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1268 1273 1268 1273 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1273 1277 1273 1277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1273 1277 1273 1277 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 56 60 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 175 179 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 420 425 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 891 895 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 922 926 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1289 1293 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1542 1546 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2044 2048 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 2103 2107 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 2442 2446 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 2569 2574 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 2693 2698 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
A cohort of 73 +/+, Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice was generated by mating nine Scn8aClth/+ siblings [generation (N5xN5)N2] in six trio matings and comprised of all mice born over several months. Phenotypic analysis was carried out using a modified SHIRPA protocol, adapted from Rogers et al. (1997). (a similar protocol can be found at ). Additional phenotyping analysis included (1) specific observations of mouse general behaviour over 1 min (assessing the presence of facial twitches, muscle spasms of the body, piloerection, shaky or unsteady movement, abnormal postures, repetitive nosepoking, hyperactivity, excess rearing); (2) fore- and back-leg grip strength using a grip strength meter (BioSeb) and (3) excess freezing behaviour occurring outside the viewing jar and the duration of freezing after the clickbox test. Due to welfare issues concerning Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice, only +/+ and Scn8aClth/+ mice were tested in the grip strength test (n = 56). Scoring of tests shown in Fig. 5 was performed as follows: wire manoeuvre: good attempt = 1, impaired attempt = 0; limbgrasping: absent = 0, present = 1; toe-pinch reflex: absent = 0, present = 1 and freezing during testing: absent = 0, present = 1. Thirty nine +/+, Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth littermate mice from the cohort were tested in the open-field and light-dark behavioural tests (five females and eight males per genotype). Open-field testing was performed as outlined on the EMPReSS website () using videotracking software analysis by EthoVision; mice were scored for latency of first movement in arena (seconds), number of movements into the centre, duration spent in centre (seconds), distance moved in arena (cm) and in centre (cm), maximum distance per move in arena (cm) and in centre (cm), mean velocity in arena (cm/seconds) and in centre (cm/seconds), duration of moving in arena (seconds) and in centre (seconds). Light-dark apparatus and software used was TruScan 99 (Coulbourne Instruments). Tests were performed between 0900 and 1400 h. Mice were tested in the same order as the open-field test. Mice were moved from the home room into a quiet acclimatization room at least 30 min before the start of the test. A clean, opaque Perspex dark box was placed into the left-hand side of the clean arena with the opening facing to the left. Red light only was used for illumination using a lamp directly above the 'lit' region of the arena. Mice were placed directly from the home cage into the opening of the dark box, and the recording was started. The time for the mouse to enter the light half of the arena (scored by all four paws placed in the light half) was recorded manually and the mouse was left undisturbed to complete the test.
###end p 23

(a) Statistical analysis for genotypic differences of weight, neurological, neuromuscular and behavioural phenotypes of Scn8aClth mice at 6, 10 and 18 weeks (n = 73), where Ft,u denotes the F-statistic on t degrees of freedom. ###begin title 25
Statistical analysis
###end title 25
###begin p 26
###xml 80 81 80 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</italic>
###xml 341 346 341 346 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">anova</sc>
###xml 365 366 365 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</italic>
###xml 1091 1092 1091 1092 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1214 1219 1214 1219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1219 1223 1219 1223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1219 1223 1219 1223 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1230 1235 1230 1235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1235 1239 1235 1239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1235 1239 1235 1239 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1240 1245 1240 1245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1245 1249 1245 1249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1245 1249 1245 1249 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 720 725 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 953 957 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 991 995 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1250 1254 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Except for ABR threshold data, which were analysed under a two-tailed Student's t-test, statistical analysis was carried out using the software package R (2005). Data was statistically analysed for a genotype effect. To adjust for confounding variables, continuous numeric data were analysed under a linear model using analysis of variance (anova) and multivariate F-test; binary data were analysed under a generalized linear model and ordinal data were analysed under a proportional odds logistic regression model. The significance of a genotype effect was tested under a model which accounted for other factors, namely, (mating identifier, sex, genotype) vs. (mating identifier, sex). Data obtained by using different mouse cohorts were analysed separately. Tests showing an 'imbalance of design' [where there was a large discrepancy in the number of individuals showing different responses within a test, e.g. in a binary (qualitative) test where 65 mice showed a positive response and 8 mice showed a negative response] were manually analysed for the distribution of values by genotype. P values were corrected for multiple hypotheses testing using the false discovery rate test (FDR, 5%). Estimate values for Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (relative to +/+) under this model were obtained, having accounted for sex and mating identifier. Tests showing significance (FDR = 5%) were further tested to find the best fit of mode of inheritance, under a 'dominant' model [(mating, sex, non-wild-type status, homozygous status) against (mating, sex, non-wild-type status)] and a 'recessive' model [(mating, sex, non-homozygous status, wild-type status) against (mating, sex, non-homozygous status)].
###end p 26
###begin title 27
Results
###end title 27
###begin title 28
###xml 33 38 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Identification of the Cloth-ears mouse mutant
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 4 14 4 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 93 99 93 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 87 104 87 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b36">Nolan <italic>et al.</italic> 2000</xref>
###xml 424 425 424 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 571 581 571 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 671 677 671 677 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 892 898 892 898 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 943 955 943 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears/+</italic>
###xml 1022 1031 1022 1031 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 1047 1056 1047 1056 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 1225 1231 1225 1231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 1236 1245 1236 1245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 1356 1365 1356 1365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 1424 1430 1424 1430 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 1502 1507 1502 1507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/</italic>
###xml 1512 1521 1512 1521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 15 20 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 57 62 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 276 281 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 582 586 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 678 682 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 872 876 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 899 903 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 956 960 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1032 1036 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1057 1061 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1218 1222 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1246 1250 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1366 1370 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1431 1435 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1522 1526 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The Cloth-ears mouse mutant was identified in a dominant mouse ENU-mutagenesis screen (Nolan et al. 2000). The founder mutant presented at 5 weeks with a reduced startle response to a 90 dB SPL, 20 kHz single tone burst, generated by a clickbox. Frozen sperm from the founder mouse was used to fertilize C3H/HeH oocytes by IVF. Startle response in offspring was assessed by clickbox test. We found that 30% of N3 offspring (n = 66) showed a mild or absent Preyer's reflex and a mild or absent startle response, confirming the genetic basis of this phenotype. A colony of Cloth-ears mice was generated for genetic mapping and phenotypic analysis by backcross of confirmed Clth/+ mice to the C3H strain. Phenotype analysis of an N4 generation backcross cohort showed that the reduced startle response was autosomally inherited, but at reduced penetrance (16 of 58 backcross mice). In addition, Clth/+ mice showed an episodic tremor (see below). Cloth-ears/+ mice with a reduced startle response were intercrossed to produce Clth/Clth mice. Putative Clth/Clth mice displayed a continuous tremor (see below) and also displayed a reduced startle response to the clickbox, but at much greater penetrance (5 of 23 intercross mice). Clth/+ and Clth/Clth mice showed a normal lifespan, no unexpected lethality and were fertile. The severity of continuous tremor in Clth/Clth mice and the frequency and severity of episodic tremor in Clth/+ mice appeared to increase moderately with age (< 2 years), but neither Clth/+ or Clth/Clth mice developed gait defects, limb weakness or paralysis at any age.
###end p 29
###begin title 30
Genetic mapping and identification of the Cloth-ears gene
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 4 14 4 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 114 120 114 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 166 176 166 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 264 272 264 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D15Mit42</italic>
###xml 277 286 277 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D15Mit246</italic>
###xml 310 317 310 317 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig01">Fig. 1a</xref>
###xml 424 433 424 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 452 458 452 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 570 580 570 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D15Mit97.2</italic>
###xml 585 594 585 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D15Mit246</italic>
###xml 660 666 660 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 667 673 667 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 779 789 779 789 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D15Mit97.2</italic>
###xml 807 816 807 816 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rs8266857</italic>
###xml 831 838 831 838 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig01">Fig. 1a</xref>
###xml 845 855 845 855 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 898 907 898 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rs4231023</italic>
###xml 932 941 932 941 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a_SNP</italic>
###xml 434 438 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 650 654 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The Cloth-ears mutation arose on a mutagenized (BALB/cAnN x C3H/HeH)F1 individual. Marker analysis of 64 affected Clth/+ backcross progeny allowed us to localize the Cloth-ears mutation to a 3.1 Mb region on distal chromosome 15 between the microsatellite markers D15Mit42 and D15Mit246 (Ensembl, version 50) (Fig. 1a), and indicated that the mutagenized chromosome was from the BALB/c strain. Moreover, genetic analysis of Clth/Clth mice derived from Clth/+ intercrosses and showing a continuous tremor refined the non-recombinant region to 1.37 Mb between the markers D15Mit97.2 and D15Mit246. Additional genotyping of non-affected (non-tremoring) mice from Clth/+xClth/+ intercrosses yielded two more recombinants that further refined the region to 1.2 Mb between the markers D15Mit97.2 at 100.63 Mb and rs8266857 at 101.83 Mb (Fig. 1a). The Cloth-ears locus was non-recombinant with the marker rs4231023 and the in-house marker Scn8a_SNP.
###end p 31

###xml 840 845 840 845 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 845 849 845 849 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 845 849 845 849 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 917 922 917 922 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 922 926 922 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 922 926 922 926 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 927 932 927 932 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

###xml 1012 1022 1012 1022 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 1344 1354 1344 1354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 1491 1513 1484 1506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b32">Meisler &amp; Kearney 2005</xref>
###xml 1860 1870 1849 1859 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 804 808 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 850 854 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 937 941 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1967 1972 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
(a) Haplotypes of backcross and intercross progeny segregating the Cloth-ears mutation. The Cloth-ears (Clth) mutation arose on a mutagenized (BALB/cAnN x C3H/HeH)F1 individual. Sixty-four backcross progeny with a reduced startle response and/or an intermittent tremor and 26 intercross progeny with or without a continuous tremor were mapped across chromosome 8 and genotyped at recombinant markers. The genetic data indicates that the mutagenized chromosome was from the BALB/cAnN strain. The Cloth-ears mutation is non-recombinant with the SNP markers Scn8a_SNP and rs4231023 and maps to the interval D15Mit97.2-rs8266857. (b) Chromatograms of the Cloth-ears mutation from wild-type (+/+) and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth DNA. Arrow: base 2942 of the Scn8a coding sequence, showing an adenine (A) in wild-type mice and a thymine (T) in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (arrow). The predicted amino acid sequence from wild-type and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice is also indicated, highlighting the D981V change. (c) Position of the Cloth-ears mutation (D981V) in the SCN8A amino acid sequence. D981V resides within the predicted domain 2 (D2) of the SCN8A peptide, six amino acids downstream of the S6 transmembrane segment. The amino acid sequence of domain 2 (D2) is shown in black; sequence of domain 2 segment 6 (D2S6) is shown in pink and the position of the Cloth-ears mutation (D981V) is shown in bold red. (d) Schematic of the voltage-gated sodium channel alpha- and beta-subunit proteins (adapted from Meisler & Kearney 2005). The alpha-subunit comprises four homologous domains (D1-D4 or DI-DIV), which are shown in different colours, each containing six transmembrane segments (S1-S6). S4 segments function as voltage sensors and the S5-S6 loops form the outer pore. A pore structure is formed by the transmembrane segments in the membrane (inset). The location of the Cloth-ears mutation is shown (red star). (e) Alignment of peptide sequences of SCN8A orthologues and other mouse SCN alpha-subunits (Ensembl) in the region of amino acid 981 (arrow). Alignments were made using clustal-W web-based software.
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 4 14 4 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 340 346 340 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Krt2-8</italic>
###xml 348 352 348 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Krt8</italic>
###xml 478 484 478 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 469 489 469 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b24">Kuijpers <italic>et al.</italic> 1992</xref>
###xml 500 506 500 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 491 511 491 511 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b33">Mogensen <italic>et al.</italic> 1998</xref>
###xml 553 555 549 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Na</italic>
###xml 555 556 551 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</italic>
###xml 555 556 551 552 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>v</italic></sub>
###xml 561 566 557 562 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 646 652 642 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 638 657 634 653 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b4">Burgess <italic>et al.</italic> 1995</xref>
###xml 671 676 667 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 747 753 743 749 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 739 758 735 754 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b22">Kohrman <italic>et al.</italic> 1996</xref>
###xml 769 775 765 771 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 760 780 756 776 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b47">Sprunger <italic>et al.</italic> 1999</xref>
###xml 830 835 826 831 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 225 230 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 242 247 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 463 467 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 677 682 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 836 841 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
The Cloth-ears non-recombinant region contains 33 genes, including a cluster of keratin genes and several novel genes. We selected candidate genes on the basis of their reported function, expression or association with known mouse mutants or human disorders. Two genes were initially selected as good candidates. The type 1 keratin 8 gene (Krt2-8, Krt8) is a component of the cytoskeleton localized to the supporting cells of the cochlear organ of Corti in adult mice (Kuijpers et al. 1992; Mogensen et al. 1998). The VGSC alpha-subunit type VIII gene (Nav1.6, Scn8a) is expressed in cerebellum, cortex and the peripheral nervous system (Burgess et al. 1995) and several Scn8a mouse mutants display intention tremor and gait defects (e.g. Kohrman et al. 1996; Sprunger et al. 1999). However, no hearing loss has been reported for Scn8a mouse mutants.
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 164 173 164 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 303 308 303 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 320 326 320 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Krt2-8</italic>
###xml 451 456 451 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 476 485 476 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 539 546 539 546 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig01">Fig. 1b</xref>
###xml 575 581 575 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 586 595 586 595 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 652 662 652 662 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 674 675 674 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 817 826 817 826 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig01">Fig. 1b,c</xref>
###xml 896 903 896 903 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig01">Fig. 1e</xref>
###xml 1039 1046 1039 1046 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig01">Fig. 1e</xref>
###xml 1196 1203 1196 1203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig01">Fig. 1d</xref>
###xml 174 178 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 486 490 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 596 600 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 940 945 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Mutation screening of coding sequence, intron-exon boundaries and 3' untranslated regions of the candidate genes was carried out by sequencing genomic DNA from two Clth/Clth mice. Sequences were compared to genomic DNA sequence from both parental strains (BALB/cAnN and C3H/HeH). Ninety-five percent of Scn8a and 90% of Krt2-8 coding sequences were analysed for mutations. An adenine to thymine tranversion was identified at base 2942 (A2942T) of the Scn8a coding sequence in Clth/Clth mice, which was not present in the parental strains (Fig. 1b). Genotyping of a cohort of Clth/+ and Clth/Clth mice showed that this mutation was 100% concordant with Cloth-ears phenotype (n = 122). This base change causes a non-synonymous amino acid change from aspartic acid to valine at residue 981 of the SCN8A peptide (D981V) (Fig. 1b,c). Residue D981 is conserved in orthologous SCN8A peptides (Ensembl) (Fig. 1e). Residue D981 is also conserved in mouse SCN1A, SCN2A1, SCN3A, SCN4A, SCN5A, SCN9A and SCN10A, but not in SCN7A and SCN11A (Ensembl) (Fig. 1e). Residue D981 lies six amino acids downstream of the predicted end of the sixth transmembrane segment of the second domain in SCN8A peptide (D2S6) (Fig. 1d). This high level of conservation and position very near to a transmembrane domain suggests an important role for D981 in sodium channel function.
###end p 34
###begin title 35
Cloth-ears does not complement a known mutant of Scn8a
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 62 72 62 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 133 138 133 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 139 140 139 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">J</italic>

###xml 249 254 249 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

###xml 427 433 427 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 419 438 419 438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b3">Buchner <italic>et al.</italic> 2004</xref>
###xml 441 447 441 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 469 474 469 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 475 476 475 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">J</italic>
###xml 474 476 474 476 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4<italic>J</italic></sup>
###xml 748 758 748 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 763 768 763 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 769 770 769 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">J</italic>
###xml 768 770 768 770 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4<italic>J</italic></sup>
###xml 790 796 790 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/+</italic>
###xml 798 803 798 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 804 805 804 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">J</italic>
###xml 803 805 803 805 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4<italic>J</italic></sup>
###xml 857 866 857 866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth/Clth</italic>
###xml 916 926 916 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 980 985 980 985 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 987 992 987 992 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 992 996 992 996 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 992 996 992 996 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 150 155 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 265 269 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 365 369 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 448 452 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 479 483 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 662 667 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 690 694 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 808 812 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To assess whether the D981V mutation in SCN8A was causing the Cloth-ears phenotype, we carried out a complementation test cross with Scn8a4J, a known mouse mutant of Scn8a. The Scn8a4J mutation is a missense mutation (Buchner et al. 2004). However, Scn8a4J/Scn8a4J mice display a much more severe phenotype, showing hindlimb paralysis and juvenile death. Scn8a4J/+ mice are not reported to show any abnormal phenotype (Buchner et al. 2004). Clth/+ mice were crossed to Scn8a4J/+ mice. Of 15 offspring, 3 showed a continuous tremor in the head and body (20%), beginning at 8-9 days old. Extended freezing and severe tremor episodes were noticeably present in one mouse. Interestingly, these mice also showed an abnormal gait. This result shows that Cloth-ears and Scn8a4J do not complement: Clth/+, Scn8a4J/+ mice show a phenotype that clearly resembles the Clth/Clth phenotype, but that is slightly more severe. The Cloth-ears mutant will be therefore referred to as an allele of Scn8a, Scn8aClth.
###end p 36
###begin title 37
###xml 11 15 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Cloth-ears mice have a reduced acoustic startle response
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 71 76 71 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 76 80 76 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 76 80 76 80 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 159 160 159 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 261 268 261 268 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig02">Fig. 2a</xref>
###xml 396 401 396 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 401 405 401 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 401 405 401 405 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 412 417 412 417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 417 421 417 421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 417 421 417 421 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 421 427 421 427 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 615 622 615 622 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Methods</italic>
###xml 624 633 624 633 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">Fig. 3a,c</xref>
###xml 708 713 708 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 713 717 713 717 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 713 717 713 717 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 827 834 827 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig03">Fig. 3c</xref>
###xml 885 890 885 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

###xml 1285 1290 1285 1290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1290 1294 1290 1294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>

###xml 1309 1315 1309 1315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1315 1319 1315 1319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1315 1319 1315 1319 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1518 1523 1518 1523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1523 1527 1523 1527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1523 1527 1523 1527 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1533 1538 1533 1538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1538 1542 1538 1542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1538 1542 1538 1542 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1542 1548 1542 1548 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1548 1552 1548 1552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1548 1552 1548 1552 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 83 87 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 116 120 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 432 436 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 718 722 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 895 899 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1192 1196 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1250 1254 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1320 1324 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1553 1557 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We assessed in more detail the onset of startle response impairment in Scn8aClth/+ mice by weekly clickbox tests of mice from an age-matched backcross cohort (n = 58). The onset of a persistently reduced startle response was found to be between 31 and 79 days (Fig. 2a). We assessed the impairment of the startle response quantitatively using startlebox analysis. At 6, 10 and 18 weeks old, both Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice showed significantly reduced amplitude of startle response to white noise at 110 dB SPL. Statistical analysis showed that the reduction in startle best fit a dominant model (see Methods; Fig. 3a,c). This result confirmed the reduced startle response that was observed in Scn8aClth mice by clickbox test. In addition, the startle amplitude progressively worsened between 6 and 10 weeks old (Fig. 3c). This suggests that the impairment of startle in Scn8aClth mice begins before 6 weeks of age and that this impairment progresses until at least 10 weeks of age, supporting the previous findings from weekly clickbox tests. No difference in latency of peak startle amplitude was found at 6, 10 or 18 weeks of age in either Scn8aClth/+ or Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (Fig. 3a). A residual startle response in almost all mice tested indicated that neither Scn8aClth/+ or Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice were profoundly deaf. However, this analysis did not rule out the possibility of a motor impairment, instead of hearing loss, as the primary cause of the reduced startle response. In addition, Scn8aClth/+ or Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice did not show evidence of vestibular impairments such as circling, headbobbing or abnormal behaviour in grid walking or swimming (data not shown).
###end p 38

(a) Statistical analysis for genotypic differences of hearing phenotypes of Scn8aClth mice at 6, 10 and 18 weeks (n = 73), where Ft,u denotes the F-statistic on t degrees of freedom. Analysis was performed under a linear model (see Methods). Startle amplitudes and maximal latencies were measured in response to 40 ms soundbursts of white noise at 110 dB SPL using the startlebox paradigm. Parameters significantly different to wild types are given with the best fit of inheritance. n.s., not significant; *P < 0.05; **P < 0.01; ***P < 0.001 (unadjusted P values). (b) Statistical analysis for genotypic differences of ABR peak latencies of Scn8aClth mice at 5-7 months old, where Ft,u denotes the F-statistic on t degrees of freedom. Analysis was performed under a linear model (see Methods). Parameters significantly different to wild types are given with the best fit of inheritance. n.s., not significant; *P < 0.05; **P < 0.01; ***P < 0.001 (unadjusted P values). (c and d) Graphical representation of significantly different startle response and ABR peak latency parameters in Scn8aClth mice compared with wild types, showing data for adjusted P values < 0.05. Startle response was measured by placing mice in a soundproof chamber containing a loudspeaker to generate sound. Startle amplitude was calculated in arbitary units using an accelerometer connected to the chamber floor to measure floor displacement upon sound presentation. Data shown are estimate values for Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice, having adjusted for sex and mating identifier, where +/+ is normalized to = 0.
