###xml 3594 3598 3587 3591 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 3600 3601 3593 3594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 73 77 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 127 131 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 355 359 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 416 420 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 555 559 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 704 708 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 971 975 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1255 1259 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1592 1596 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1978 1982 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2034 2038 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2077 2081 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2230 2234 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2273 2277 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2446 2450 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2786 2790 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2890 2894 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 3110 3114 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 3178 3182 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 3607 3611 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
(a) Age of onset and penetrance of reduced startle response in Scn8aClth mice. Startle response analysis of 58 age-matched, N4 mice from a (Clth/+x +/+) cross, comprising ungenotyped Scn8aClth/+ and +/+ progeny, showed that 27.6% of the cohort display a reduced startle response to a 90 dB SPL, 20 kHz single tone burst, indicating reduced penetrance. As mice are ungenotyped, these data include both +/+ and Clth/+ mice. The onset of reduced startle response was between 31 and 79 days. (b) Representative histology of middle and inner ears of Scn8aClth mice. No morphological differences in structure, size or bone density of middle ear ossicles from 6-10-month-old Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice were seen (scale bar, 1 mm). The small protusion on the stapes seen in the +/+ sample has detached with the incus during dissection in the Scn8aClth/+ sample. H&E-stained 8 mum dorsal sections of the middle ear of 8-month-old Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice shows that the middle ear cavity is free from effusive matter and the epithelium is smooth, indicating the absence of otitis media, and the tympanic membrane is intact (scale bar, 500 mum). H&E-stained 5 mum cochlear sections from 6-month-old Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice shows a normal organ of Corti (OHC, outer hair cell; IHC, inner hair cell; TM, tectorial membrane; RM, Reissner's membrane; scale bar, 100 mum). In some samples, Reissner's membrane has detached during processing. Scanning electron microscopy of the exposed organ of Corti from 6- to 7-month-old Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice shows three rows of OHCs and IHCs in all samples (scale bar, 8 mum). No patterning abnormalities or degeneration of stereocilia or hair cells was seen. Some artefacts of sample preparation can be seen (spherical blebs) in +/+ and mutant samples. (c) Mean and SEM of ABR hearing thresholds of 3-month-old sex-matched +/+ (n = 7), Scn8aClth/+ (n = 7) and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth (n = 8) mice at 8, 12, 20 and 26 kHz. Thresholds of Scn8aClth/+ mice were significantly different from +/+ mice at 8 kHz (Scn8aClth/+ vs. +/+: 8 kHz, P = 0.0363; 12 kHz, P = 0.2570; 20 kHz, P = 0.3288 and 26 kHz, P = 0.5602). Thresholds of Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice were significantly different from +/+ mice across all four frequencies tested (Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth vs. +/+: 8 kHz, P = 0.0007; 12 kHz, P = 0.0006; 20 kHz, P = 0.0071 and 26 kHz, P = 0.0342). Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice showed an average threshold increase of 10-14 dB SPL. Significance levels are indicated in pink for Scn8aClth/+ and in blue for Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth. n.s., not significant; *P < 0.05; **P < 0.01; ***P < 0.001. (d) Representative ABR traces from 5-7-month-old sex-matched +/+ (n = 5), Scn8aClth/+ (n = 5) and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth (n = 5) mice at 80, 70, 60 and 50 dB SPL to 8 kHz tones. Peaks 1-5 are labelled I-V. ABR of Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice shows a merged morphology of peaks 3 and 4, and peak 4 shows a smaller amplitude than peak 3. Peaks 3-4 and 4-5 interpeak latencies appear prolonged. At 60 and 50 dB SPL, a response is seen from Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice, but peaks are much less defined than from +/+ and Scn8aClth/+ mice. (e) Threshold curves (mean +/- SD ) for DPOAE at frequency 2f1-f2. The horizontal axis is f2 frequency. The vertical axis is the level of f1 to generate emission of 0 dB SPL. Level of f2 was 10 dB below the f1 level. Ratio f2/f1 was 1.23. Red symbols represent mean values for +/+ (n = 3), magenta symbols represent mean values for Scn8aClth/+ (n = 6) and blue symbols represent mean values for Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth (n = 4) mice. There was no significant difference between the three genotypes at any frequency tested
###end p 40

Cloth-ears mice display ABR abnormalities indicative of a peripheral neural auditory defect

###xml 675 679 675 679 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 23 27 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 191 195 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 351 355 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 408 412 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 510 514 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 591 595 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 680 684 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We examined Cloth-ears mice for hearing loss by ABR analysis. To determine auditory thresholds, ABR analysis was performed on sex-matched 3-month-old +/+, Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (n = 22) at decreasing dB SPL levels from 90 dB SPL at 8, 12, 20 and 26 kHz (Fig. 2c). Statistical analysis showed that auditory thresholds of Scn8aClth/+ mice were only significantly increased compared with +/+ mice at 8 kHz, but that Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth thresholds were significantly increased compared with +/+ mice across the four frequencies tested (see figure legend). Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice showed an average threshold increase of 10-14 dB SPL. This indicates that Scn8aClth mice have mild semi-dominant hearing loss.
###end p 42

###xml 1118 1125 1118 1125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig02">Fig. 2b</xref>
###xml 1180 1185 1180 1185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

###xml 1185 1189 1185 1189 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1196 1201 1196 1201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1201 1205 1201 1205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1201 1205 1201 1205 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1206 1211 1206 1211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1211 1215 1211 1215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1211 1215 1211 1215 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 68 72 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 320 324 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 511 515 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 760 764 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 975 979 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1101 1105 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1110 1116 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 1216 1220 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To investigate the pathological causes of hearing loss in Scn8aClth mice, we examined auditory structures including the outer, middle and inner ears and the peripheral neural auditory pathway. Dissection and X-ray analysis of the middle ear ossicles of 6-10-month-old Scn8aClth/+ (n = 2) and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth (n = 2) mice showed no malformations compared to controls (Fig. 2b). Haemotoxylin and eosin (H&E)-stained sections of middle ears from 8-month-old Scn8aClth/+ (n = 2) and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth (n = 2) mice did not show any differences to controls, with normal middle ear epithelia, intact tympanic membranes and no evidence of otitis media (Fig. 2b). H&E-stained cochlear sections from 6-month-old Scn8aClth/+ (n = 2) and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth (n = 2) mice showed no structural abnormalities in the organ of Corti (Fig. 2b). In addition, scanning electron microscopy (SEM) of cochlear hair cells from 6-7 month-old Scn8aClth/+ (n = 2) and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth (n = 2) mice showed no mispatterning of the stereocilia or degeneration of hair cells, two common pathologies of hearing loss in both mice and humans (Fig. 2b). Gross cochlear structure and outer ear structure in Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice were also normal (data not shown).
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 88 93 88 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 93 97 93 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 93 97 93 97 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 431 436 431 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 436 440 436 440 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 436 440 436 440 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 447 452 447 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 452 456 452 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 452 456 452 456 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 456 462 456 462 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 462 466 462 466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>

###xml 2321 2325 2321 2325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 2321 2325 2321 2325 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 2527 2537 2527 2537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b17">Henry 1979</xref>

###xml 2627 2631 2627 2631 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 2674 2684 2674 2684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 2758 2779 2758 2779 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b43">Robles &amp; Ruggero 2001</xref>
###xml 2870 2875 2870 2875 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 2875 2879 2875 2879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 2875 2879 2875 2879 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 2879 2885 2879 2885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 2885 2889 2885 2889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 2885 2889 2885 2889 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 2891 2892 2891 2892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 2899 2904 2899 2904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 2904 2908 2904 2908 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 2904 2908 2904 2908 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 2912 2913 2912 2913 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 2928 2929 2928 2929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 2941 2948 2941 2948 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig02">Fig. 2e</xref>
###xml 3064 3071 3064 3071 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig02">Fig. 2e</xref>
###xml 3128 3134 3128 3134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 3118 3139 3118 3139 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b26">Lukashkin <italic>et al.</italic> 2007</xref>
###xml 3194 3204 3194 3204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 98 102 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 467 471 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 653 657 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 814 818 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 892 896 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1142 1146 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1295 1299 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1324 1328 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2295 2299 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2328 2332 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2632 2636 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2685 2689 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2830 2834 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2935 2939 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 3205 3209 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The lack of an obvious peripheral structural defect (in outer, middle or inner ears) in Scn8aClth mice led us to extend our ABR analyses and focus on possible deficits in higher peripheral neural auditory regions. A typical ABR waveform is composed of five peaks, corresponding to electrical signals generated by different components of the peripheral auditory pathway. ABR analysis was performed on sex-matched 5-7-month-old +/+, Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (n = 15) using 90 dB SPL tones at 8, 12, 20 and 32 kHz, and peak latencies were statistically analysed for differences (Figs. 2d and 3b,d). Both Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice showed no differences in latency of peak 1 (Fig. 3b,d), thought to represent cochlea and cochlear nerve function (Henry 1979). However, Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice displayed abnormal waveform morphology from peak 3 compared with control mice: peaks 3 and 4 showed a merged morphology, with peak 4 showing a smaller amplitude than peak 3, and peaks 3-4 and 4-5 interpeak latencies appeared prolonged (Figs. 2d and 3b,d). In addition, peak 5 was often almost absent in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice. Statistical analysis of peak latencies showed that many interpeak measurements were significantly different in Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice compared with wild-type mice (Fig. 3b,d). We found that peak 1-5 latency was indeed significantly prolonged, suggesting a recessive model, in response to all frequencies tested (8, 12, 20, 32 kHz). Given the abnormal wave morphology of peaks 3-5, we looked in more detail at peak 3-5 latencies. Peak 3-5 and 4-5 latencies were also significantly prolonged, at different frequencies (Fig. 3b,d), which may reflect different sensitivities of the ABR technique. Of particular interest is the significant prolongation of peak 3-5 latency at 20 kHz, which best fits a dominant inheritance model. As our statistical model did not account for semi-dominant inheritance, examination of the estimate values for this parameter suggests that a semi-dominant model may better fit these results (peak 3-5 latency: Scn8aClth/+ = +0.525 msec, Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth = +0.842 msec; Fig. 3d). Overall, these results suggest that ABR peak latency between peaks 3 and 5 is prolonged, certainly in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice and probably in Scn8aClth/+ mice. Peaks 3, 4 and 5 of the ABR are thought to correspond to retrocochlear neural regions of the auditory pathway [probably the superior olivary complex, lateral lemniscus and inferior colliculus (Henry 1979)]. These analyses suggested that peripheral neural auditory function is abnormal in Scn8aClth mice. To confirm that the hearing loss in Cloth-ears mice was not caused by dysfunction of the cochlear amplifier and, hence (Robles & Ruggero 2001) the outer hair cell function was normal in these mice, we measured DPOAEs in 6-month-old Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth (n = 4), Scn8aClth/+ (n = 6) and +/+ (n = 3) mice (Fig. 2e). Distortion product otoacoustic emission thresholds were not significantly different between the three genotypes (Fig. 2e), indicating that normal power amplification (Lukashkin et al. 2007) of the cochlear mechanical responses is preserved in Cloth-ears mice.
###end p 44
###begin title 45
###xml 11 15 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Cloth-ears mice display tremor and paroxysmal movement abnormalities
###end title 45
###begin p 46
###xml 48 53 48 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 53 57 53 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 53 57 53 57 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 92 97 92 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 97 101 97 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 97 101 97 101 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 58 62 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 104 108 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 338 342 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 457 461 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 536 540 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 570 574 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
An additional motor phenotype was identified in Scn8aClth mice. Initially, we observed that Scn8aClth/+ mice displayed an episodic, complex phenotype of extended freezing behaviour, piloerection, a hunched posture and an intermittent side-to-side coarse tremor of the whole body. This phenotype was observed at the earliest in 25-day-old mice. Similarly to the reduced startle response, this phenotype was observed at reduced penetrance (15 of 58 backcross mice), and each component of the phenotype was not always observed in the same mice. However, 25 of 58 backcross mice had either a reduced startle response and/or episodic tremor (43.1%), suggesting that the same underlying mutation was variably affecting both auditory and neurological/neuromuscular function.
###end p 46
###begin p 47
###xml 13 18 13 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 18 22 18 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 18 22 18 22 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 22 28 22 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 28 32 28 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 28 32 28 32 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 286 291 286 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 291 295 291 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 291 295 291 295 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 301 306 301 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 306 310 306 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 306 310 306 310 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 310 316 310 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 316 320 316 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 316 320 316 320 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>

###xml 1103 1108 1103 1108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

###xml 1108 1112 1108 1112 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1119 1124 1119 1124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1124 1128 1124 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1124 1128 1124 1128 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1128 1134 1128 1134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1134 1138 1134 1138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1134 1138 1134 1138 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 33 37 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 76 80 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 212 216 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 321 325 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 362 366 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 435 439 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 557 561 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 683 687 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 923 927 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1016 1020 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1139 1143 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
In addition, Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice showed a more severe phenotype. These mice displayed a continuous and coarse tremor of the head and body, from 8 days old. Tremor was observed in both stationary and walking mice. However, no gait abnormalities were observed in either young or old Scn8aClth/+ or Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice. Interestingly, Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice also showed the extended freezing behaviour observed in Scn8aClth/+ mice, coincident with piloerection and hunched posture. During these freezing episodes, the tremor of Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice was also observed to increase in severity and amplitude, strongly resembling the episodic tremor episodes of Scn8aClth/+ mice. Also, tremor amplitude and the duration of behavioural arrest often increased following behavioural testing, suggesting that stress could be affecting this phenotype. Therefore, we observed two distinct tremor phenotypes in Scn8aClth mice, firstly a recessive continuous tremor affecting general posture in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice and secondarily a dominant episodic tremor with behavioural arrest affecting both Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice.

###xml 1592 1601 1592 1601 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5a,c</xref>
###xml 1675 1680 1675 1680 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

###xml 1691 1696 1691 1696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1696 1700 1696 1700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1696 1700 1696 1700 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1700 1706 1700 1706 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1706 1710 1706 1710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1706 1710 1706 1710 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1717 1718 1717 1718 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 63 67 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 245 249 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 591 595 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 858 862 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1037 1041 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1315 1319 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1586 1590 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1711 1715 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1772 1776 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We assessed if the tremor and motor abnormalities in Scn8aClth mice could be associated with muscular, cerebellar or other tissue changes. Sections of semimembranosus and quadriceps muscles from 8.5-month-old Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (n = 4) showed no differences to wild-type muscles in H&E-stained sections. Specifically, there was no evidence of degenerative or regenerative changes (fibre size asymmetry, pyknotic nuclei, centrally nucleated fibres; data not shown). We also examined H&E-stained cerebellar sections from 8.5-month-old Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (n = 4) that showed no indication of Purkinje cell loss or disorganization of the trilaminar structure (Fig. 4a). To quantify any potential abnormalities of the mutant cerebellum further, we examined sections of 8.5-month-old Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice using cresyl violet staining (n = 4) (Fig. 4a). Cerebellar dimension and layer measurements and Purkinje cell counts showed that although cerebellum from Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice are slightly smaller than +/+ and Scn8aClth/+ animals and show a slightly reduced number of Purkinje cells, the ratio of the PCL to GCL width is normal, suggesting the overall structural development and maintenance of the cerebellum are not affected in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (Fig. 4b). Furthermore, no neuronal mislocalization was observed and the lamination of the cortex and hippocampus appeared normal in all sections examined, thus the small Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth cerebellar differences are likely to reflect the overall small size of the mice (Fig. 5a,c). H&E-stained sections of 33 other tissues and organs from 8.5-month-old Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (n = 4) showed no histological differences to wild-type mice (data not shown). Peripheral (sciatic) nerves showed no abnormal myelination and spinal cord sections showed no abnormalities (data not shown).
###end p 48

###xml 344 348 343 347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 344 348 343 347 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 364 369 363 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

(a) H&E-stained coronal sections of cerebellum from 8-month-old mice show no Purkinje cell loss in any region (scale bar, 50 mum). Histopathology of the cerebellum of 8.5-month-old mice using cresyl violet on coronal sections shows no neuronal mislocalization (scale bar, 1 mm). (b) Area and layer measurements and Purkinje cell counts of Scn8aClth mice. Although Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth cerebellums are slightly smaller and show slightly reduced Purkinje cell counts compared with +/+ and Scn8aClth/+, the Purkinje cell layer (PCL) to granule cell layer (GCL) ratio is normal, indicating normal overall cerebellar structure. Area measurements are in millimetres. (c) Abnormal dystonic postures displayed by Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice during recovery from anaesthesia were not seen in +/+ or Scn8aClth/+ mice. Postures were maintained for up to 1 min.

###xml 75 79 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 190 194 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 285 289 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Lastly, we noticed that the response to anaesthesia in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice was abnormal. During recovery from anaesthesia (ketamine/medetomidine) after ABR testing, Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice displayed abnormal dystonic postures (n = 5) that were not observed in Scn8aClth/+ or +/+ mice (Fig. 4c), and a longer time to regain normal movement (data not shown).
###end p 50

###xml 1988 1995 1988 1995 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5a</xref>
###xml 2043 2048 2043 2048 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

###xml 2226 2231 2226 2231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 2231 2235 2231 2235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 2231 2235 2231 2235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 2261 2270 2261 2270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5a,c</xref>
###xml 2361 2368 2361 2368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5a</xref>
###xml 63 67 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 123 127 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 230 234 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 368 372 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 925 929 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1091 1095 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1307 1311 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1536 1540 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1590 1594 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1742 1746 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1799 1803 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2063 2067 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2154 2158 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2236 2240 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The unusual motor symptoms and freezing behaviour in Scn8aClth mice led us to investigate the gross phenotype of Scn8aClth mice by detailed phenotypic and behavioural testing of +/+, Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth littermate mice at 6, 10 and 18 weeks of age (n = 73). These time-points spanned the ages at which these phenotypes appeared to develop in Scn8aClth mice. Data was statistically analysed for a genotype effect. To adjust for confounding variables, continuous numeric data were analysed under a linear model using anova and multivariate F-test; binary data were analysed under a generalized linear model and ordinal data were analysed under a proportional odds logistic regression model (see Methods for further information). Parameters showing a significant difference were further analysed to determine the best fit of inheritance (dominant or recessive) (see Methods). This analysis showed that Scn8aClth mice show significant dominant, recessive, and probably semi-dominant abnormalities in growth, neurological and motor function and behaviour. The weight of Scn8aClth mice was significantly less than wild type at all ages tested (Fig. 5a,c), with statistical analysis suggesting both recessive (6 weeks, 10 weeks) and dominant (18 weeks) inheritance. Estimate values for Scn8aClth/+ mice were intermediate between wild-type and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth values (Fig. 5c), suggesting that growth retardation is likely to be semi-dominant. Grip strength in (1) forelegs and (2) all legs was not different in Scn8aClth/+ mice at any age tested (Fig. 5a). Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice were not tested using the grip strength test for welfare reasons. Ability to perform the wire manoeuvre test was recessively impaired in Scn8aClth mice at 6, 10 and 18 weeks of age (Fig. 5a,c). Scn8aClth mice also showed recessive increased tendency to limb grasp (Fig. 5a,c). Trunk curling during tail suspension was not successfully analysed statistically because of experimental imbalance (Fig. 5a), but individual test results showed that most Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice displayed abnormal trunk curling behaviour, instead of the splayed limbs of wild-type mice (data not shown). The toe-pinch reflex was recessively impaired in Scn8aClth mice at all ages tested (Fig. 5a,c). However, proximal reflex tests of corneal, pinna and reaching reflexes were all normal (Fig. 5a).
###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 75 82 75 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Methods</italic>
###xml 85 90 85 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 90 94 90 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 90 94 90 94 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 183 192 183 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5a,c</xref>
###xml 340 349 340 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5a,c</xref>
###xml 387 392 387 392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 392 396 392 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 392 396 392 396 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 43 47 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 95 99 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 282 286 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 397 401 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 416 420 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We assessed general behaviour by observing mice undisturbed for 1 min (see Methods). Scn8aClth mice showed a recessive increased tendency to freeze during testing at all ages tested (Fig. 5a,c) and a recessive increased duration of freezing after the clickbox test (where wild-type mice normally freeze for 1-2 seconds) at 10 and 18 weeks (Fig. 5a,c). No significant differences between Scn8aClth mice and wild-type mice were found in facial twitching, muscle spasms of body, piloerection, shaky or unsteady movement, abnormal postures, repetitive nosepoking, visible hyperactivity or excessive rearing (data not shown).
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 31 36 31 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 36 40 36 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 36 40 36 40 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 47 52 47 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 52 56 52 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 52 56 52 56 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 57 62 57 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 62 66 62 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 62 66 62 66 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 100 105 100 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 105 109 105 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 105 109 105 109 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 204 209 204 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 209 213 209 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 209 213 209 213 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 220 225 220 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 225 229 225 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 225 229 225 229 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 229 235 229 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 235 239 235 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 235 239 235 239 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 246 247 246 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 305 310 305 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 310 314 310 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 310 314 310 314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 493 500 493 500 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5b</xref>
###xml 623 628 623 628 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 628 632 628 632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 628 632 628 632 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 632 638 632 638 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 638 642 638 642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 638 642 638 642 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 649 658 649 658 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="fig05">Fig. 5b,d</xref>
###xml 67 71 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 110 114 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 240 244 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 315 319 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 487 491 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 643 647 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The freezing behaviour in both Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice raised the possibility that Scn8aClth mice could suffer high anxiety. We tested anxiety and locomotion in 5-6-month-old sex-matched Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (n = 39) using the open-field and light-dark box paradigms. Scn8aClth mice did not show any significant differences in any parameters tested in the open-field test, indicating no observed anxiety or locomotion defects compared with wild-type mice (Fig. 5b). However, the latency of first entrance into the lit half of the light-dark box was significantly recessively reduced in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice (Fig. 5b,d).
###end p 54
###begin title 55
Discussion
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 49 59 49 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 61 66 61 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 66 70 66 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 66 70 66 70 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 216 221 216 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 35 40 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
We report that a novel ENU-induced mouse mutant, Cloth-ears (Scn8aClth), shows hearing loss with peripheral neural auditory impairment as well as paroxysmal motor symptoms and tremor, and that a missense mutation in Scn8a underlies this phenotype. The data suggests that SCN8A is critical for normal peripheral auditory function and may play a role in the pathogenesis of paroxysmal motor disorders.
###end p 56
###begin title 57
###xml 5 9 5 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 5 9 5 9 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 10 14 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Scn8aClth mice are a model of peripheral neural hearing loss
###end title 57
###begin p 58

###xml 1503 1508 1503 1508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>

###xml 1508 1514 1508 1514 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>med</italic>&#8722;<italic>jo</italic></sup>

###xml 1673 1674 1673 1674 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">J</italic>
###xml 1669 1674 1669 1674 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>med</italic>&#8722;<italic>J</italic></sup>
###xml 1676 1681 1676 1681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scnm1</italic>
###xml 1681 1682 1681 1682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 1681 1682 1681 1682 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>R</italic></sup>
###xml 1682 1688 1682 1688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scnm1</italic>
###xml 1688 1689 1688 1689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 1688 1689 1688 1689 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>R</italic></sup>
###xml 1713 1719 1713 1719 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1708 1724 1708 1724 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b20">Koay <italic>et al.</italic> 2002</xref>
###xml 1762 1772 1762 1772 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 1878 1883 1878 1883 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 2010 2015 2010 2015 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 2015 2019 2015 2019 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 2015 2019 2015 2019 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 2103 2113 2103 2113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 2170 2175 2170 2175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 99 103 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 271 275 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 369 373 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 677 681 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1089 1094 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1527 1531 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1607 1612 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1691 1695 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2020 2024 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 2212 2216 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
We did not detect any morphological or functional pathology in middle or inner ears from Scn8aClth mice by histology, ABR and DPOAE analysis, showing that the Scn8aClth mutation does not affect middle ear or cochlear function. However, ABR analysis showed that Scn8aClth mice have abnormal morphology of peaks 3-5 and lengthened peak latencies. Peaks 1-5 of the ABR in mice are generally considered to arise approximately from the cochlear origins (peak 1), from the cochlear nucleus (peak 2), the superior olivary complex (peak 3), the lateral lemniscus (peak 4) and the inferior colliculus (peak 5) (Henry 1979). Our findings suggested that the auditory deficit in Scn8aClth mice is caused by a peripheral neural defect originating from the superior olivary complex, lateral lemniscus or inferior colliculus (peaks 3, 4 and 5, respectively), although these generators of the ABR are still contested (Henry 1979). This suggests that SCN8A is involved in auditory nerve and peripheral neural auditory function. SCN8A is localized to the organ of Corti and cochlear ganglionic axons in the mouse, and has been shown to be involved in the generation and regeneration of action potentials in cochlear ganglion cells (Hossain et al. 2005). Interestingly, a role for Scn8a in the central auditory pathway was previously suggested (Chen et al. 1999) by observation of greatly reduced spontaneous bursting activity of neurons in the dorsal cochlear nucleus (DCN) in brain slices from Scn8amed-J/Scn8amed-J and Scn8amed-jo/Scn8amed-jo mice. However, no hearing impairment has been previously reported for any Scn8a mouse mutants, and indeed hearing in dystonic Scn8amed-J/Scn8amed-J (Scnm1R/Scnm1R) mice was normal (Koay et al. 2002). Therefore, it is possible that the Cloth-ears mutation represents a unique gain-of-function allele in the auditory system. Thus, reassessment of other Scn8a alleles for subtle hearing deficits would be merited. Further histological and functional analysis of the auditory pathway in Scn8aClth mice would identify which structures are primarily, and secondarily, affected. The Cloth-ears mutant is therefore the first evidence that mutation in Scn8a can result in hearing impairment in mice.
###end p 58
###begin title 59
###xml 23 27 23 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>

###xml 961 965 961 965 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 961 965 961 965 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1029 1034 1029 1034 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1063 1068 1063 1068 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1068 1071 1068 1071 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med</italic>
###xml 1072 1074 1072 1074 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">jo</italic>
###xml 1068 1074 1068 1074 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>med</italic>&#8722;<italic>jo</italic></sup>
###xml 1075 1080 1075 1080 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1080 1083 1080 1083 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med</italic>
###xml 1084 1086 1084 1086 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">jo</italic>
###xml 1080 1086 1080 1086 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>med</italic>&#8722;<italic>jo</italic></sup>

###xml 1141 1157 1141 1157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b10">Dick <italic>et al.</italic> 1985</xref>
###xml 1272 1277 1272 1277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1277 1281 1277 1281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1277 1281 1277 1281 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1281 1287 1281 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1287 1291 1287 1291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1287 1291 1287 1291 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1348 1353 1348 1353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1477 1483 1477 1483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1471 1488 1471 1488 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b41">Raman <italic>et al.</italic> 1997</xref>
###xml 1571 1592 1571 1592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b11">Duchen &amp; Stefani 1971</xref>
###xml 1685 1706 1685 1706 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b11">Duchen &amp; Stefani 1971</xref>
###xml 1876 1881 1876 1881 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1881 1885 1881 1885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1881 1885 1881 1885 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 1885 1891 1885 1891 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1891 1895 1891 1895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1891 1895 1891 1895 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 20 24 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 240 244 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 559 564 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 708 712 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 824 829 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 966 970 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1087 1091 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1292 1296 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1354 1359 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1896 1900 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice begin to display a continuous tremor at 8 days old, and later, show impairment at the wire manoeuvre test and the distal toe-pinch reflex, that suggests muscle weakness and distal sensory loss is occurring in these mice. The onset of skeletal muscle weakness or paralysis in the lethal Scn8a mutants is also from around 8 days old (Buchner et al. 2004; Duchen & Strich 1966; Lane 1976). Moreover, Garcia et al. (1998) showed that SCN8A was responsible for the threefold increase in sodium current between postnatal day 0 and day 8 in mouse motor neurons, and suggested that this was caused by postnatal upregulation of Scn8a. Thus, the onset of motor symptoms in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice correlates with the reported upregulation of Scn8a in motor neurons. In contrast to almost all published Scn8a mouse mutants, we did not observe degenerative changes in skeletal muscle, cerebellum or any gait defects or paralysis in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice. Particularly, this is markedly different to a non-lethal Scn8a mutant that shows a tremor: Scn8amed-jo/Scn8amed-jo mice have a marked loss of cerebellar Purkinje cells (Dick et al. 1985). A functional but mild impairment of one or more of these tissues could therefore underlie the motor deficits in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice. Functional abnormalities previously identified in Scn8a mouse mutants include a loss of resurgent sodium current and disrupted firing patterns in cerebellar Purkinje cells (Raman et al. 1997), reduced conduction velocity and a prolonged refractory period in motor neurons (Duchen & Stefani 1971) and a failure of muscle fibres to show action potentials in response to nerve stimulation (Duchen & Stefani 1971). Electromyography/electophysiological analysis of muscle, motor neurons and cerebellar output would be needed to delineate the origins of tremor and muscle weakness in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice.
###end p 60
###begin title 61
###xml 31 35 31 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 31 35 31 35 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 41 45 41 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 41 45 41 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 46 50 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Behavioural phenotypes in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice
###end title 61
###begin p 62
###xml 5 10 5 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 10 14 10 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 10 14 10 14 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 26 31 26 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 31 35 31 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 31 35 31 35 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 35 41 35 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 41 45 41 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 41 45 41 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 547 552 547 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN4A</italic>
###xml 657 662 657 662 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 748 753 748 753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn2a</italic>
###xml 762 768 762 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 755 773 755 773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b28">Martin <italic>et al.</italic> 2007</xref>
###xml 804 809 804 809 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 809 813 809 813 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 809 813 809 813 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 17 21 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 46 50 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 437 441 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 446 452 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 483 488 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 559 563 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">OMIM</span>
###xml 637 641 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">OMIM</span>
###xml 732 737 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 816 820 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1252 1256 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Both Scn8aClth/+ mice and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice display an episodic tremor with behavioural arrest phenotype. This similarity of phenotype and its infrequent nature suggests that this is a dominant episodic phenotype occurring under particular external or internal conditions that could be seizure- or dystonia-like. Genetic and non-genetic factors are known to moderate some paroxysmal (episodic) neurological and motor disorders in mice and humans. For example, myotonia in the human disorder paramyotonia congenita caused by mutation in the SCN4A gene (OMIM: #168300) is aggravated and/or induced by exposure to cold temperatures (OMIM). Indeed, even Scn8a has recently been reported to modulate the severity of seizures in a mouse mutant of Scn2a (Martin et al. 2007). We tested a small cohort of Scn8aClth/+ mice to see if handling or auditory testing induced tremor episodes, but only a small increase in tremor occurrence was observed (data not shown), indicating that these stimuli were not major inducers of tremor. Robust testing of the effect on tremor occurrence of other environmental factors such as temperature, and crossing to different genetic backgrounds, would be useful in isolating the precipitators of tremor episodes in these mice.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 32 37 32 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 37 41 37 41 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 48 53 48 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 53 57 53 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 53 57 53 57 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 58 63 58 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 63 67 63 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 63 67 63 67 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 234 239 234 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 239 243 239 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 239 243 239 243 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 243 249 243 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 249 253 249 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 249 253 249 253 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 391 396 391 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 400 406 400 406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 406 410 406 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 406 410 406 410 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 556 561 556 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 561 565 561 565 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 561 565 561 565 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 585 590 585 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 590 594 590 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 590 594 590 594 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 594 600 594 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">/Scn8a</italic>
###xml 600 604 600 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 600 604 600 604 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 755 760 755 760 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 760 763 760 763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med</italic>
###xml 764 767 764 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TgA</italic>
###xml 768 770 768 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bs</italic>
###xml 760 770 760 770 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>med</italic>&#8722;<italic>TgA</italic>4<italic>Bs</italic></sup>
###xml 771 776 771 776 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 776 779 776 779 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">med</italic>
###xml 780 783 780 783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TgA</italic>
###xml 784 786 784 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bs</italic>
###xml 776 786 776 786 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>med</italic>&#8722;<italic>TgA</italic>4<italic>Bs</italic></sup>
###xml 801 807 801 807 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 793 812 793 812 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b21">Kohrman <italic>et al.</italic> 1995</xref>
###xml 870 876 870 876 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 861 881 861 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b5">Caldwell <italic>et al.</italic> 2000</xref>
###xml 1003 1008 1003 1008 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1146 1152 1146 1152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1137 1157 1137 1157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b31">McKinney <italic>et al.</italic> 2008</xref>
###xml 1266 1276 1266 1276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cloth-ears</italic>
###xml 1347 1352 1347 1352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN8A</italic>
###xml 1406 1412 1406 1412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1398 1417 1398 1417 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b49">Trudeau <italic>et al.</italic> 2006</xref>
###xml 1451 1456 1451 1456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCN8A</italic>
###xml 1531 1537 1531 1537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 1521 1542 1521 1542 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="b51">Wasserman <italic>et al.</italic> 2005</xref>
###xml 1661 1666 1661 1666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
###xml 1666 1670 1666 1670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 1666 1670 1666 1670 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 68 72 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 254 258 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 411 415 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 441 445 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 566 570 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 605 609 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 705 710 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 787 791 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 964 968 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1490 1496 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 1671 1675 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Alternatively, it could be that Scn8aClth/+ and Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice have heightened anxiety, leading to increased freezing (behavioural arrest). We found that the incidence and duration of freezing was significantly increased in Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice by visual observation. However, the decreased time of latency of first move into the light-half in the light-dark paradigm shown by Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice could suggest that these mice show lessened anxiety. Open-field analysis did not show any differences in locomotion and anxiety measures of Scn8aClth mice. Furthermore, Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice displayed a greater frequency of trunk curling and limb grasping, which are often displayed by mouse mutants with neurological defects including Scn8amed-TgA4Bs/Scn8amed-TgA4Bs mice (Kohrman et al. 1995). SCN8A is highly expressed in the hippocampus (Caldwell et al. 2000), which is involved in fear-related behavior. Recently, it has been reported that mice heterozygous for a null allele of Scn8a show evidence of 'emotional' behavioural defects, including increased freezing and avoidance of the centre in open-field tests (McKinney et al. 2008). This study indicates that, for some behavioural phenotypes, the null heterozygote is more severe than the Cloth-ears allele described here. In addition, the only family identified with a SCN8A mutation show neuropsychological impairment (Trudeau et al. 2006). A positive association between SCN8A variants and suicide attempts in humans has also been reported (Wasserman et al. 2005). It would be interesting to assess if a seizure-like or anxiety phenotype underlies the behavioural abnormalities in Scn8aClth mice by electroencephalography and further behavioural testing.
###end p 63

###xml 2186 2191 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 2387 2392 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 2657 2663 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">infant</span>
Complementation testing showed that the Asp981Val mutation in SCN8A underlies the Scn8aClth phenotype. Voltage-gated sodium channels are transmembrane proteins that allow fast influx of sodium ions into excitable cells in response to membrane depolarization, and are responsible, among other functions, for generating and conducting action potentials (reviewed in Ogata & Ohishi 2002). The widespread expression of Scn8a in the central and peripheral nervous system (Caldwell et al. 2000) and the critical function of SCN8A in generating sodium currents in neurons (Cummins et al. 2005; Garcia et al. 1998; Raman et al. 1997) suggest that functional defects in neuronal excitability could be responsible for the auditory defects, tremor and neurological/behavioural defects of Scn8aClth mice. It is possible that the Asp981Val amino acid substitution causes a change in SCN8A channel kinetics or sodium current properties. Electrophysiology on another Scn8a mouse mutant with tremor [Scn8amed-jo/Scn8amed-jo (Ala1071Thr)] showed that the Scn8amed-jo mutation caused a shift in the voltage dependence of SCN8A channel activation (Kohrman et al. 1996), which could decrease neuronal excitability and thus result in ataxia and tremor. Additionally, the close proximity of the Asp981Val amino acid change to the predicted end of the D2-S6 segment (Fig. 1d) suggests that it is possible that this residue could be involved in the function of domain 2. Indeed, several mutations in the D2-S6 segment of the rat Scn2a have been shown to affect channel kinetics, including altering the voltage dependence of activation and inactivation, and causing incomplete inactivation (Yarov-Yarovoy et al. 2002). Also, we found that Scn8aClth/Scn8aClth mice showed abnormal dystonic postures after anaesthesia, that were not seen in Scn8aClth/+ and wild-type mice. Interestingly, residues in the D2-S6 segment have been shown to be involved in the binding and action of anaesthetics to VGSCs (Kondratiev & Tomaselli 2003; Wang et al. 2001). Additionally, several amino acid mutations in other VGSC alpha-subunit genes that lie in very close proximity to the Asp981 amino acid have been identified in four human disorders. Functional consequences of these mutations include changes in fast inactivation and persistent currents (Green et al. 1998; Schwartz et al. 2000). Intriguingly, symptoms in these four human disorders are episodic, and believed or known to be precipitated by external or internal stimuli: the paroxysmal muscular disorders, paramyotonia congenita/myotonia congenita and myotonia fluctuans (SCN4A) (McClatchey et al. 1992; Ricker et al. 1994); near-sudden infant death syndrome (SIDS) caused by the cardiac condition long QT syndrome type 3 (LQT3) (SCN5A) (Schwartz et al. 2000) and severe myoclonic epilepsy of infancy (SMEI) (SCN1A) (Claes et al. 2001; Escayg et al. 2000). Thus, we predict that the Scn8aClth Asp981Val mutation could alter SCN8A channel kinetics or sodium current properties in Scn8aClth neurons, which could be assessed in vitro and in vivo.
###end p 65
###begin title 66
###xml 9 13 9 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Clth</italic>
###xml 9 13 9 13 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>Clth</italic></sup>
###xml 14 19 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 47 52 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
The Scn8aClth mouse is a resource for studying human disease
###end title 66
###begin p 67
###xml 4 9 4 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Scn8a</italic>
